< review>
Ordered burrito and got charged for stake chips, whatever, but I took one bite of my burrito and I had to spit it into my napkin. I threw the whole thing in the garbage. I'm no foodie, I eat from food trucks, gas stations, and holes in the wall.... Also I'm what they call Gordo "fat"... So for me to throw $11 away worth of food is telling.

The issue: the smell of the food. I bit Into the burrito, and was hit a smell that I can describe as a mix of 3 day old roadkill with Petaluma manure smell from cow farms. I hate to be mean, but this is so far off from what I would expect to be sold from a business. For those who have had "gamey" meat, you may understand, it was a gamey smell that almost instantly made me convulse. I hope this was just a "bad day" and someone accidentally recycled unrefrigerated food or something... I cannot fathom how anyone who experienced what I got could ever return.</review>

< Review>
I have been here twice with my cat, and one time to pick up food. The doctor and staff are knowledgeable and kind. They put the animal needs and best interest first. He does not run any more tests than necessary at that time, and makes suggestions of what and when follow ups may be needed. You take the initiative to call for test results and future appointments. You don't actually have a set appointment. You call to found out the hours the doctor will be seeing patients and take your pet in. It is also a pet hospital, at other times he is doing procedures.
I've never had a long wait with a waiting room full of pets and people.</Review>

Alexa always made herself available to answer any questions I had along the way.

Apartment pros:
- Amenities include: a basketball court, ping pong, a rock climbing wall, a pool table, and 2 gyms (with class schedules)

Cons:
- The rent is on the higher end, but I‚Äôd say it‚Äôs well worth it with the amenities and proximity to necessities

Don't rent during the pandemic! They are using predatory sales tactics during the market downturn which will result in you getting a worse deal than everyone else at other buildings. Read on for a short description why.

The fine print says the rent price during the lease includes two months free. This is to circumvent the sf rental pricing laws that prevent rental increases of more than 0.7% each year. This place will give you the advertised price for the lease term, and then leave you with a whopping 14% increase in rent at the end. Your rent will go up by $$$ hundreds when everyone else has theirs go up by less than $50.

< Review>
We loved our time here.  We had a Studio on the 18th floor of Phase 3 with a beautiful view of the bay and the Giants stadium.  The staff is friendly, and access to 280 South is really easy.  My only issue is the ventilation of the apartment.  There are only 2 small windows that open.  They are on the same wall, so there is no chance for cross breeze.  The apartment is on the leeward side of the building, so no natural breeze, and no AC.  We stuck 2 small fans that fit in the windows, but still the apartment was really warm during the relatively cool summer. The heatwaves we had made it almost unbearable.  The place is expensive, but so is the rest of the area, so I feel it's in line with the rest of the apartments.  This place is worth looking at.  They are very flexible with lease terms and pet friendly, which was a big selling point for us.<//Review>

<Text>I lived here, in phase 3, for 4 years, and recently moved out not because of this complex, but because I no longer liked San Francisco.

For the location, size, and amenities, this place was a remarkable deal. Like most Avalon communities, the initial price is relatively low then they raise the rent by high amounts, but with negotiation this is kept to reasonable rent increases that reflect the market. AT&T fiber is available in phase 3, without a data cap.

The concierge team is all star. They're super kind and helpful, and they got to know me by name pretty quickly.

I had an apartment facing the courtyard, and rarely heard the trains. Fourth and King St is a big transportation hub with the Caltrain station, so relative to bay area transit it is fast, though expect regular, major bus/tram delays. With the freeway right next door, exiting the city by car is super easy and there's zipcars you can use to do so.

The downsides of this complex are all pretty much that it's in San Francisco, though the neighborhood is, for San Francisco, very nice. As with all of SF, lots of homeless, and human urine and feces to dodge every time you walk outside. Lots of solicitors, both political (in those seasons) and religious, will bother you if you stand outside too long. Severe understaffing meaning quality of services goes drastically down (expect to visit concierge or contact maintenance a second time occasionally for the same task). Were this rating not relative to San Francisco, I'd give this place 2/5 stars.

Move out was very smooth. I did move to another Avalon, so that and my long stay may have factored in, but they offered a cheap move-out cleaning service, and did not charge me for painting the walls or replacing the carpets (sadly, had pet damage on each). I received, less the cleaning service fees I opted into, my full security deposit back, without any hassle.

If I were forced to return to San Francisco, I'd pick this community again.</Text><Resp>{'time': 1569436662510, 'text': "Thank you for sharing your whole experience with us, Kir. We'll take all of your feedback under advisement as we try to improve where needed while we keep up the good parts everywhere else."}</Resp>< user_name>

You won't regret choosing Avalon at Mission Bay! This is now my second time living here, and I'm extremely happy. Let me break down why I like Avalon:

Front Desk: I'm in phase 1, and the front desk staff are always very polite and courteous. Very different from MANY buildings. < text>
My fiance and I stayed at the Avalon during the summer of 2016 and we loved the building.Though a little pricey (what isnt in SF though?), the amenities and location more than make up for it. The community has 2 gyms, bbq area, indoor basketball court, sky lounge, 24 hr concierge, and several community rooms, one with a very unique climbing wall! There's also free coffee everyday and free tickets to Giants games available periodically to residents.

The location is excellent with extremely easy access to all sorts of transit (2 muni lines, Caltrain, and bus).  It was nice that the Avalon has 3 buildings that we could access - I think this allowed for a greater number of amenities to be available to the community.

The staff was extremely attentive throughout our short 3 month stay and renting furniture through their partner Brooks made our move in and move out seamless.  If circumstances bring us back to the area, we would definitely consider living here again!<//text>
<date>1473871704603<//date></record></dataset><record>
<Text>My wife, our little furball and I moved to Avalon Mission Bay North from Manhattan back in 2014.

Undeniably the community's location is second to none, offering quick access to grocery stores, public transportation, parks and speedy access to the highway.
Given that my wife works from home, going the extra mile for housing made a lot of sense, particularly given the presence of an onsite gym and of a 24/7 concierge desk.

I am not going to lie, our first year at Avalon ended up being rocky as we ran into several issues, ranging from loud neighbors, break-ins inside the low rise where we were initially living in, to second hand cigarette smoke infiltrating our apartment. While I am at it, I'd say that in some areas of the community, apartments are filled with young kids rooming together, which gives a noisy college dorm style to the community.
Thankfully, a few months after our 2nd move within the community, things have turned out for the best and we are looking forward to renewing our lease.

Most importantly, I wanted to give a shout out to a few folks that over the past 2 years have gone above and beyond. In no particular order:

- Danilo Baldoza: top notch technician, always gets things done at the first maintenance visit. Specifically, thank you for making up for the sloppy work from a previous technician and getting our window sealing replaced correctly.
- Javier Carpio: extremely courteous person, always smiling when running into him in the elevator or in the hallways.
- Elizabeth Castro: she has a special place in our hearts, as she is always all about to our little furball.
- Marisol Cothern: professional and conscientious member of the staff. She follows through, is dilligent and always with a smile. We are glad to have you with us.
- Christian Manuel: courteous, always gets stuff done right off the bat and always with a big smile.
- Jai Meiers: he is the man. Enough said.
- Raymond Mitra: extremely sweet and helpful. Thank you for all those morning smiles.
- Cristine Rodriguez: our #1 community consultant, hands down. She nailed our 2nd lease and we are looking forward to working with her again.
- Rommel Santo Domingo: extremely dedicated to his work, effectively delivering stunning service across the board.
- Jason Sypult: Jason saved us from many community related issues. Namely, my wife and I always talk about how he was able to bring the second hand smoke issue we faced to an end.

Thank you all for delivering spectacular service!</Text>< user_name>
Siamac M< /user_name>

<review>I lived here for 4 years and absolutely loved the experience.

The price is a bit steep, but then again we all have come to expect that in the gentrified parts of San Francisco right. The fittings are good but not really great (phase 3 and properties across the street are a bit better in that regard), but when you add the price and quality up it comes down to a good value for money.

What's really easy to love about this place is that the Safeway is right across the street, some of the best restaurants of SF are all in walking distance, the Caltrain and 2 muni lines and dozens of busses all stop right at that block - so your commute into the city or down to the valley will be shorter then ever.

There's also Genentech, Google, Facebook and so on shuttles right there since they all stop at the Caltrain station - so it doesn't really get better then that.< /review>< Pics>

<Review>Choosing to live at Beach City has proved to be one of the best choices I've made. When I first decided to attend SBCC, I was especially anxious about what my living situation would be like since I was coming alone. After living here for almost two years, I can honestly claim that Beach City is the perfect situation for all students who are either first years or new to the area. It puts them in an environment that makes it so easy to meet those people you'll want to get a house with afterwards, instead of risking sharing a lease with strangers from craigslist.  Everyone who lives here attends SBCC so it's incredibly social and like it's own little bubble (you can't not make friends here!), it's ridiculously close to the school (2min walk), and basically in center of anything you'll ever need (groceries, beach, downtown, etc.). Management is always very friendly and the maintenance requests I've put in has always been fixed within 3 days. It's also clear that management has been doing nothing but making changes for the better, like creating a new study lounge and throwing events every single week that almost always involves free food! The initial experience was fine. We spoke with Kara the first day who was who was helpful. The following business day she was not there and let us know Jack would be the one helping us. From there he gave me a call and let me know what they thought needed to be done with the car and that the parts would take some time to come. There were 2 parts that he said needed replaced. A file pump and a fuel pump module. He explained to me that replacing a module when you replace the pump was equivalent to the oil filter when you change the oil, you just always do it. Problem being that it is a 200$ part so I was reluctant to accept a routine part swap at 200$. After the conversation I spoke with multiple other mechanics who said that wasn't the case but I chalked it up to him having expertise I don't so I didn't keep pushing it. The problem arose when I was on KBB looking at the resale value of the car (kind of over the car) and it prompts me there might be a recall on that model. Come to find out after putting in the specific Vin for my vehicle it was a recall for....the module. Immediately I called and spoke to jack again and thankfully caught them before they had began work. I explained on KBB it said there might be a recall so before they continue I wanted to be positive.
